It is now scheduled to end today, and the second crackdown will be scheduled later.

Appeal Documents Should Be Submitted to the Court of First Instance 108

The Procuratorate of the First Special District Court Issues a Public Notice Explaining that They Should Not Be Submitted Directly to the Court of Appeal

The Procuratorate of the Shanghai First Special District Local Court issued a public notice yesterday, stating: For the purpose of public notice, the Shanghai Jiangsu High Court Second Branch Procuratorate issued Instruction Jian Zi No. 141, which forwarded the Supreme Court Procuratorate Instruction Ping Zi No. 2610, which stated: In cases of appeal to the Supreme Court, the appeal or reasoning documents should be submitted to the court of first instance in accordance with the law, and should not be mistakenly presented directly to the Supreme Court Procuratorate. The relevant legal provisions and points to be noted should be explained in detail and widely publicized. Therefore, after investigation, Article 342, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law stipulates that "To file an appeal, an appeal document shall be submitted to the court of first instance." The so-called court of first instance refers to the court of original judgment. When appealing to the High Court or its branch, the Local Court is the court of first instance. When appealing to the Supreme Court, the High Court or its branch is the court of first instance. Furthermore, Article 374, Paragraph 1 of the same law stipulates that "The appeal document shall state the reasons for the appeal. If the reasons are not stated, a written statement of reasons shall be submitted to the court of first instance within ten days after the appeal is filed." Since this article is stipulated in the chapter on the third instance of the same law, the so-called court of first instance specifically refers to the High Court or its branch. Furthermore, to file an appeal, the appeal document shall be submitted to the court of first instance within ten days after the service of the judgment, as stipulated in Articles 341 and 342 of the same law. If the appeal document for appeal to the third instance does not state the reasons, a written statement of reasons shall be submitted to the court of first instance within ten days after the appeal is filed, as clearly stipulated in Article 374 of the same law. All of these are the legal procedures regarding appeal. If the appeal document is not submitted within the statutory period, or the written statement of reasons is not submitted to the court of first instance, or even if it is submitted to the court of appeal within the statutory period, but not submitted to the court of first instance, resulting in a delay of the appeal period before it is submitted to the court of first instance, all of these violate the statutory procedures and will be subject to the court's ruling to dismiss the appeal, as clearly stipulated in Articles 376 and 387 of the Criminal Procedure Law. In accordance with the foregoing instruction, the above articles are hereby explained and publicized for general knowledge. The parties concerned must pay special attention to the above-mentioned statutory procedures in the future. When filing an appeal, the appeal document shall be submitted to the court of first instance and shall not be submitted directly to the court of appeal, in order to comply with the procedures and safeguard the right to sue. This is of utmost importance. This is a public notice.

Direct Dialing in the Chinese Concession is Not True 109

The Ministry of Interior Consults with Provincial and Municipal Governments to Consider Pilot Programs for Female Police Officers 110

The Ministry of Interior believes that training women as police officers has long been recognized as effective by the League of Nations Committee on Trafficking in Women and Children, which has advised member states to adopt it. It has also resolved to urge countries without female police officers to try pilot programs. In the past, there have been no such female police officers in China. In recent years, as social interactions between men and women have gradually become more open and social conditions have become increasingly complex, ignorant women in domestic commercial metropolises are inevitably exploited by others to commit crimes, thereby endangering public security. If the patrol depends solely on male police officers, it is difficult to be thorough. In order to cope with the social environment, it is necessary to establish female police officers. The Capital Police Department and the Shanghai Public Security Bureau have successively piloted female inspectors, which have already achieved remarkable results. Therefore, other provinces and cities should follow up and establish them to meet environmental needs and maintain social tranquility. The Police Administration Department has formulated concrete measures and sent them to provincial and municipal governments, instructing their subordinate police agencies at all levels to consider the situation in their respective jurisdictions and try to implement them.

The drawings and applied materials for these three vessels have been provided by the bureau and sent to shipyards in Shanghai for bidding. It is now certain that the tenders for the two upstream motor vessels have been submitted by various shipyards to the bureau, where they will be examined by the New Vessel Committee and the Chief Shipowner's Shipbuilding Department. A decision on the winning shipyard will be made in about a week. The purchase of materials has also been ordered. The price of each vessel has increased by one-third compared to the original bidding price, costing approximately 300,000 yuan per vessel, totaling 600,000 gold yuan for the two vessels. The official bidding papers will be selected in one week and submitted to the ministry for approval. The construction will then be ordered. The bidding papers for the new Yangtze River vessel have been scheduled to be opened on January 15th of next year.

The Head Chef of a Warship Arrested for Private Possession of Silver Coins 113

After the Ministry of Finance of the National Government promulgated the regulations prohibiting the export of silver currency, customs officers have repeatedly seized violators, but the amounts were only between 100 to 200 yuan and 300 to 400 yuan. However, last month, over 1,700 yuan in silver dollars were seized on a warship of a certain country. The person who privately carried the money was Tan Shiquan, the head chef of the warship (commonly known as the chief purser). On October 5th of this year, the warship arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong. After arriving at the port, customs officer Gu Renmin boarded the ship for inspection as usual and seized 1,300 Hong Kong silver coins from Tan. The captain of the ship proved that the money was for purchasing goods, so he was exempt from further investigation. On the morning of the 7th, customs officer Wang went to the ship for inspection again and seized 1,400 Chinese silver coins from Tan's bedroom. The silver coins were taken to the customs for confiscation. At the same time, the water police station dispatched detective Huang Songsheng to arrest Tan and send him to the local court's prosecutor's office for questioning. He was prosecuted in the criminal court for obstructing the national currency. At 10:00 AM yesterday, Judge Wu Deying opened the court for interrogation. First, customs officer Gu Renmin and others stated the circumstances of the seizure. Tan Shiquan, who was in custody, stated that he was 16 years old and from Guangdong. The silver dollars were owed by the sailors of the warship for food and goods. After the ship arrived in Shanghai and received wages, the goods were repaid. He was intercepted by the customs officer and had no desire to profit. Moreover, the warship was ordered to be stationed in Shanghai and would not sail elsewhere. He asked for leniency. The judge ordered a second hearing, and the defendant was returned to custody.

All municipal smoking cessation institutions in this city consistently provide free services to inpatients undergoing treatment, without charging any fees. National Buddhist Association To Hold Memorial Service For Master Mingdao Tomorrow Morning 118

Remains to be Cremated at Lingyan Mountain in Suzhou Tomorrow Morning; Friends and Relatives Plan to Build a Pagoda in West Lake to Commemorate

Master Mingdao, a standing director of the Chinese Buddhist Association, passed away at Baoguo Temple in Suzhou at half-past noon on the 14th of this month. According to his will, his body will be cremated and his ashes mixed with flour and thrown into the sea. His eldest son, Mr. Qi Zaiyu, who works at the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, rushed to Suzhou upon hearing the news. On the 15th, he followed Buddhist rituals to enshrine the body in a coffin, and on the 16th, the coffin was taken to the body-offering kiln at Lingyan Mountain in Mutuo. The cremation is scheduled for half-past two tomorrow morning (the 21st). The general office of the Chinese Buddhist Association in this city decided at its 16th standing committee meeting the day before yesterday to hold a memorial service at Jueyuan on Hed Road at 10 AM tomorrow, with offerings and chanting throughout the day to commemorate him. His family will hold a family memorial service outside the South Gate of Jiaxing on the 4th of next month. It is also said that the master's former friends, considering the master's significant contributions to the Buddhist cause and his indelible merits, have proposed preserving his ashes and building a pagoda in the sacred land of West Lake to perpetuate his memory. The site selection and design are currently underway, and construction is expected to begin at the end of the year. A large-scale public burial ceremony will be held at that time, and a commemorative album will be published to pay tribute. According to records, the master's secular surname was Qi, his given name was Zezhou, and his Dharma name was Mingdao. He was from Jiaxing, Zhejiang. In the late Qing Dynasty, he studied at the Japanese Police Academy. After returning to China, he engaged in revolutionary activities with Chu Fucheng and others. He made great contributions to the restoration of Qing provinces. He served as the county magistrate of Tongxiang, Deqing, and Linhai in Zhejiang Province and Lingxiao County in Fujian Province. In middle age, he converted to Buddhism and specialized in the Pure Land Sect. He was tonsured in the fourteenth year of the Republic and served as a standing director of the National Buddhist Association, traveling extensively and tirelessly. He suffered from a liver ailment a month ago, which ultimately led to his death at the age of fifty-five. He had two sons and three daughters. During his lifetime, he studied Buddhism extensively and wrote many works, which are scattered in various places and have not been compiled. The Buddhist Association and his sons plan to collect the master's writings and compile them into a volume to commemorate him. If anyone has any of the master's writings, whether fragments or full pieces, they can be sent directly to the general office of the Chinese Buddhist Association on Hed Road in this city or to Qi Zaiyu at the Wuxiandian Radio Station on Minguo Road.

Candle Industry Requests French Municipal Council to Correct Fines 120

The Candle Industry Trade Association of this city recently expressed outrage at the French Concession Municipal Council's unwarranted fines imposed on its member Zhizhonghe Store and unanimously requested the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to argue the case based on reason. The original letter is as follows: "Respectfully informing you, we have recently received a letter from our member Zhizhonghe Store on Jixiang Street, stating that on the 14th of this month, a Western police officer from the French Public Works Bureau, upon seeing firecrackers displayed in the store window, deemed them unsalable and ordered them to be stored away. Although our store knew that the concession authorities had not previously issued any such prohibition, we had no choice but to comply and immediately stored the firecrackers to avoid further trouble. However, the next day, the Public Works Bureau suddenly sent a patrolman to the store to demand a fine of one yuan, and issued a receipt. This was a strange and perplexing matter. Our store has been operating in the concession for many years. Even during martial law in previous years, firecrackers and other similar items were never prohibited from being displayed in the store. Even if such interference were permissible, our compliance in storing the firecrackers should have been sufficient. Why impose a fine in addition? Moreover, firecrackers are legitimate items used for celebrations during festivals. Except during periods of alert, there is no reason for a long-term ban. Now that there is no clear prohibition and the fine is unwarranted, how can law-abiding merchants feel secure in their businesses? Therefore, we respectfully write to your Chamber, requesting that you argue the case with the French Public Works Bureau, seeking a clear explanation and a guarantee that similar incidents will not occur in the future. This is deeply appreciated."

Municipal Federation Submits Request to Social Affairs Bureau to Restrict Silver Coin Exchange Rate 121

After the Ministry of Finance announced on the 4th of this month that the banknotes of the Central Bank of China and the Bank of Communications would be designated as legal tender, it immediately set the legal tender exchange rate, stipulating that each legal tender could be exchanged for 300 copper coins and 12 jiao coins. However, small money exchange houses and tobacco shops in this city, in addition to exchanging copper coins at a rate of 297-298 per yuan, are experiencing a great shortage of silver dollars on the market. Yesterday, the exchange rate was only 10 jiao and 27-28 copper coins for each legal tender. Each double dime was exchanged for 48-49 copper coins in the Shanghai West area, 49 or 50 copper coins in the British Concession area, and 52 copper coins in the French Concession area. Based on the lowest exchange rate, one yuan of legal tender would lose more than 300 copper coins when exchanged for jiao coins and copper coins.

The Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of this city submitted an urgent request to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, asking them to crack down on the practice of merchants hoarding silver coins and to address the highly uneven exchange rates displayed in the market. The original request stated, "Regarding the urgent request, since the Ministry of Finance issued the announcement on the reform of the currency system on the 3rd of this month, there was a brief period of chaos in the market, but it was short-lived and quickly returned to normal. However, unscrupulous merchants have been engaging in greedy and despicable practices. Recently, there have been rumors of hoarding silver coins, resulting in highly uneven exchange rates displayed by tobacco and exchange businesses in the market, gradually decreasing from the stipulated price of 12 jiao to below 11 jiao, and sometimes even 10 jiao and 300 copper coins. The implementation of legal tender has initially stabilized the people's hearts, but unscrupulous merchants dare to create this chaotic market, disrupting people's minds. This must be cracked down on urgently. We hereby submit this request to your bureau, urging you to work with the Public Security Bureau to restrict market prices, stabilize people's minds, and severely crack down on criminals to get to the root of the problem. Whether this is appropriate or not is subject to your approval."

The Cypress Wax Industry Trade Association of this city convened a representative meeting the day before yesterday, with more than ten representatives, including He Yinsheng, in attendance. Mr. He was elected as the chairman. Mr. He began by reporting that the bills from Hankou dealers still used the old Baowen custom and added the names Daiping and Xiaoping, and that the Weng's office in Tianjin increased the weight of two catties of wood, making it difficult to bear. The original letter is as follows: "Respectfully informing you, we received your letter on the 10th of this month, stating that the intention of the seller is to cancel the weight of two catties of virtual wood, and that the stone is still measured according to the old custom, distinguishing between light and heavy. Your association convened its members some time ago and discussed the matter repeatedly. It was unanimously agreed that if the Hankou letter wants to use weights, it should uniformly use the nationally recognized market weights, and the weights of (Jing), (Jin), (Ma), and (Chai Gui) should all use market weights, and the silver standard should be immediately abolished and replaced with legal tender for calculation, in order to emphasize compliance with the law. The names Daiping and Xiaoping should also be abolished to avoid complications. Please reply separately. The record is on file. Li Changrong and Others Trafficking Narcotics with Five Locations 133

Li and others escaped upon hearing the news; three offenders arrested and awaiting sentencing.

Wang Shidong, a Chinese detective of the Xinzha patrol, had previously received a tip from an informant and arrested Zhang Wangshi, a woman from Wuxi, for selling red pills. Several thousand red pills were seized on the spot. After rigorous interrogation at the police station, she confessed that the narcotics were entrusted to her by Li Changrong, Wang Shunfa, and others from No. 1 Sun Temple, Sun Lane, Zhabei, to be smuggled to No. 10 Gaozhao Lane, Xinzha Road, in the Public Concession, and handed over to Xu Guihe, Li Changrong's concubine, for resale. Upon receiving this information, the police immediately dispatched detectives to search No. 10 Gaozhao Lane, where they found only Xu Guihe's younger brother, Xu Jinfa, as Xu Guihe had gone out. Xu Jinfa was taken into custody and, after repeated questioning, confessed that his sister, Xu Guihe, was currently at Peide Lane, Xinzha Road. The detectives rushed to wait for her and soon spotted her at the intersection of Carter Road. They arrested Xu and took her back to the police station along with Xu Jinfa. An investigation revealed that Li Changrong and Wang Shunfa's narcotics operation was extensive, with a total of five locations. In addition to Sun Lane in Zhabei, there was also No. 48 Sande Lane, Avenue Messager, No. 167 Peide Lane, Xinzha Road, No. 74 Chengxin Lane, Hebei Road, and No. 10 Gaozhao Lane, Xinzha Road. This clearly demonstrated their disregard for the law and the deep harm they caused. However, since the main culprits, Li Changrong and Wang Shunfa, had already escaped upon hearing the news, the arrested Zhang Wangshi, Xu Guihe, and Xu Jinfa, along with the 9,100 red pills and drug paraphernalia seized, were handed over by the police to the First Special District Court yesterday morning in accordance with Article 257 of the Criminal Code for transporting opium substitutes. Judge Liu Yugui presided over the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, presented the case and requested that Zhang and others be punished accordingly. To further substantiate the case, Gao Zhushi, a female offender who had already been convicted of selling red pills, was brought from the Western Jail to testify. Gao Zhushi had previously confessed that she had obtained the red pills from Li Changrong at No. 10 Gaozhao Lane, Xinzha Road. After Judge Liu questioned her in detail, he determined that the case was clear and ordered the defendants to be returned to custody after the conclusion of the debate, pending official sentencing next Thursday. The police are currently investigating the escaped main culprits, Li Changrong and Wang Shunfa.

Lu Xingyuan and Qiu Hanping, Two Lawyers in a Lawsuit Settlement 139

Each side presents a grand debate, a war of words; the court orders sentencing next Tuesday afternoon.

Lu Xingyuan, who once served as the President of the Provisional Court and the Seventh Court and is now a lawyer, and Shi Zhinan (also known as Shi Yuankai), who is currently an assistant at the Salt Inspectorate, were accused by Ouyang Shunying, the wife of the deceased Wang Yaochen (also known as Wang Youyu), a nominal French national from Xiamen, and represented by lawyer Qiu Hanping, of criminally prosecuting Du Ruizhen, Wang's concubine, for forging Wang Yaochen's will in Lu's office and forging Wang Yaochen's signature in the First Special District Court, requesting legal punishment. After the case was opened, Lu Xingyuan, in addition to jointly filing a counterclaim against Ouyang Shunying with Shi Zhinan, requesting that she be punished for false accusation, Lu also filed a separate criminal lawsuit against lawyer Qiu Hanping for false accusation, instigation of false accusation, and defamation. Judge Wu Zehan of the First Special District Court had summoned Lu for questioning, as reported previously. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu formally opened the court, summoned both plaintiffs and defendants, as well as witnesses, to the court for investigation. First, Qiu Hanping's defense and the attached counterclaim against Lu Xingyuan for false accusation were given to Lu to read in court. Lu then immediately stated the intent of prosecuting Qiu for three charges, stating that before September 3, Qiu reported to the Jing'an Temple Police that he, Shi Zhinan, and Du Ruizhen had colluded to forge Wang Yaochen's will and divide his estate, requesting a public prosecution. After the police sent Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate and found out that he had previously served as the president of this court and that Du Ruizhen had sold the property on Avenue Petain, they did not accept the case due to lack of evidence. Qiu then drafted a complaint on behalf of Ouyang Shunying and filed a private prosecution against them with the court. Although Qiu claimed to have reported to the police on behalf of Wang Ouyang, Wang did not go in person, and there were many arbitrary exaggerations and contradictions in the complaint. Therefore, Qiu's report to the police was a false accusation, and drafting an untrue complaint was instigation of false accusation. Leaking the contents of the complaint to newspapers constituted public insult and was intended to damage his reputation. Defendant Qiu Hanping stated that he reported to the police on September 2 on behalf of his client, Wang Ouyang, based on her instructions. In the month of this year, Wang and Du Ruizhen were involved in a lawsuit in Xiamen, and it was mentioned in the appeal that the will was forged. She then sent her nephew to Shanghai to entrust him to handle the matter and successively sent documents. Later, the police requested the original will as evidence, but the original was in Du Ruizhen's hands, so they did not file a public prosecution. Wang Ouyang then came to Shanghai in person to conduct a private assessment. The case has been opened several times, and the plaintiff has repeatedly appeared in court to state her case. If there was indeed a suspicion of instigating private prosecution, he would have been reported by the judge hearing the case without waiting for Lu Xingyuan to file a lawsuit. He had nothing to do with the newspaper publishing the matter. Although Lu pointed out that the manuscript was sent by him, there was no evidence. If he were to use such strong words and unreasonable arguments, he could also say that he did not know about the previous hearing of the case, but all the newspapers published it the next day, so he could say that Lu leaked it. As for the issue of Ouyang's nationality, she had mentioned it in court during the hearing of Shi Zhinan's lawsuit against her for debt on September 24. Lu Xingyuan was Shi's agent at the time and heard it in court, but now he suddenly said that her raising the issue of nationality was to avoid being subjected to false accusations and that it was instigated by him, completely ignoring the facts and arbitrarily making a judgment, and should dismiss the lawsuit and punish him for false accusation. Wang Ouyang also testified in court, stating that she did not know about the will until Du Ruizhen and others requested registration at the Xiamen French Consulate on March 17. In July, after learning that the property on Avenue Petain had been sold, she sent her nephew to Shanghai to investigate and immediately entrusted lawyer Qiu to handle the matter. First she reported to the police and then filed a private prosecution, all of which came from her intentions, and this claim had been decided in Xiamen. Although she had never studied, she could recognize her husband's handwriting, and the signature on the will was definitely not signed by her husband. The court then handed over the replies from various newspapers to Lu for review and informed him that the newspapers' reports were based on reports from their own reporters. Lu claimed that Qiu had given the complaint to the reporters in the audience to copy, but Qiu pointed out that it was speculation. The court then ordered the debate to begin. Lu first debated at length, first describing his past history, then talking about Qiu's various bad behaviors on behalf of Wang Ouyang, with many curses, and finally requesting that Qiu be sentenced to up to seven years of imprisonment for false accusation, saying that he must have his hair shaved and be made a prisoner, and should not be lenient. Qiu then rebutted, ignoring Lu's village woman's street cursing attitude, and refuting the accusations one by one, and also requesting that Lu be punished for false accusation. After the debate, the court adjourned and announced that the sentence would be announced at 2:00 PM on the 22nd.

National Leprosy Conference Concludes Successfully 140

Eight Important Cases Passed; Wu Zhijian Speaks After Returning to Shanghai

A National News Agency reporter met yesterday with Mr. Wu Zhijian, Secretary-General of the China Leprosy Relief Association, who gave a detailed account of the Second National Leprosy Conference held in Guangzhou. According to him, the conference was held on November 8th and 9th, following the closing of the National Medical Conference. The first day was for experts to review proposals, and the second day was for speeches by guests and officials from various fields, including Director Wen Taihua representing Commander-in-Chief Chen Jitang, Section Chief Wei Lesi representing Civil Affairs Director Lin Yizhong, Guangzhou Health Bureau Director Dr. Deng Zhende, Mr. Ma Le of the Macau Health Bureau, and Hong Kong Health Bureau Director Dr. Weilin Deng, as well as representatives from various provinces, totaling more than a hundred people. A total of eight resolutions were passed at the conference, including: (1) Requesting the Central Health Department to select physicians to study the latest leprosy medicines abroad for them to return to the country and implement; (2) Requesting the Central Health Department to forward to the provincial and municipal governments of each province to provide financial assistance to established leprosy hospitals or clinics, half of the original funding, in order to provide subsidies; (3) Requesting the provincial and municipal governments of each province to instruct their subordinate leprosy hospitals to establish more clinics, stipulate dates, and notify leprosy patients to come to the clinics for diagnosis and treatment in order to popularize the service; (4) Requesting the conference to ask the National Medical Association to organize a medical committee in order to arouse the medical community's attention to the leprosy issue; (5) Requesting the conference to submit to the Central Government to instruct the Health Department to establish a leprosy specialty in the near future in order to study and deal with all issues related to leprosy and achieve unified leadership; (6) Requesting the Central Government to promptly promulgate the leprosy decree, for leprosy patients to be protected and not discriminated against from other patients; (7) Requesting the Ministry of Education to stipulate any day of each year as "Leprosy Day" to promote national awareness; (8) Submitting to the Ministry of Education to instruct all schools to add leprosy courses so that people can have a deeper understanding. Overall, the conference went extremely well. Mr. Wu also said that the Guangzhou Municipal Government is currently preparing a relatively large-scale leprosy hospital, limited to be established by the end of this year. The Provincial Government has allocated 50,000 yuan to cooperate with the Municipal Government to establish an even larger leprosy hospital that can accommodate 1,000 patients. This plan can also be realized next year, which shows that the government is determined to eradicate the leprosy problem. Finally, the reporter asked when the new leprosy sanatorium built by the association in Dachang Town, Shanghai, would open. According to him, they are actively arranging the interior and rushing to print invitations. Once the arrangements are in place, the opening ceremony will be held around the end of this month, and patients will be admitted at the same time.

Rent Receipts Split into Two; Illegal Reduction of Housing Tax 141

Kuang Baoying and others accused; the tenant's whereabouts unknown.

The Kuang Baoying and Kuang Menghuai brothers from Wuxi have many properties in Shanghai and have set up the Kuang Zhongji Rental Accounting Office to manage them. On March 1 last year, the rental housing company signed a lease agreement with Zhao Jinbao, renting the house at No. 21 Meiren Lane, Hankou Road, to open the Yourixin Xieji Bathhouse for a term of three years at a monthly rent of 300 yuan. Zhao wanted to reduce the one-quarter housing tax paid to the Public Works Department. Since paying the tax based on the rent amount would require 42 yuan per month, he negotiated with the landlord. The rental accounting office split the 300 yuan monthly rent receipt into two, each stating a rent of 150 yuan. Zhao concealed one of the receipts and used the other as the tax payment standard, only paying 21 yuan per month. The Public Works Department Tax Office initially did not know about the cheating and had no objections. Only this autumn, Zhao Jinbao was unable to operate due to owing too much rent and was sued by the landlord. He transferred the bathhouse to Wang Fangyuan and others, renaming it Xinji. According to the rent receipts transferred by Zhao, they paid the landlord a rent of 150 yuan per month. The rental accounting office rejected this, demanding a monthly rent of 200 yuan. Wang complained that the rent was too high and demanded a rent reduction. The landlord told them that the rent receipts had been changed in the past, only half the rent amount was filled in, invisibly reducing the housing tax expenditure, which was enough to offset the rent reduction, and refused to reduce the rent further. This led to a dispute between the landlord and the tenant. Later, this secret behavior of illegally reducing housing tax was revealed. The Tax Office reported to the Chief Inspector's Office, which sent detective Chen Yonggui to investigate and confirm the facts. The Public Works Department filed a lawsuit against Kuang Baoying and Kuang Menghuai for helping Zhao Jinshi illegally reduce housing tax, requesting punishment according to Articles 339 and 30 of the Prohibitory Law. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court issued summonses. Zhao Jinbao had already disappeared. Kuang Baoying also failed to appear, so only Kuang Menghuai surrendered. The Public Works Department lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated the process of the defendant helping the tenant illegally reduce the tax and presented the rent receipts issued by the Kuang Zhongji Rental Accounting Office and the judgment of the defendant suing Zhao Jinbao for rent arrears, proving that the rent of the house now leased by Wang Fangyuan was indeed 300 yuan per month. Judge Dai questioned the defendant Kuang Menghuai and ordered a retrial at a later date.

Qu Zhibu Hospital Performs Laparotomy

According to the National News Agency, Shi Zhizhi, a Ningbo native residing at the customs declaration office at No. 10 Penglai Road, Nanshi, works at the joint venture of the "Made in China Paper Plate" company on the Public Concession race course. In October of the sixth year of the Republic of China, he was introduced to marry Zhou Rongli (also known as Zhou), a woman from his hometown, who is now 36 years old. They have not had any children. It is learned that Mrs. Shi Zhou's abdomen gradually swelled in the eighth year of the Republic of China, but her diet, daily life, and monthly menstruation were normal. During the "January 28th Incident" in Shanghai, she requested treatment from the Qu Zhibu Hospital on Penglai Road. After examination by Dr. Ye Xincheng of the hospital, it was determined that surgery was necessary to cut open the abdomen and remove the growth. At that time, the situation was unstable, so the surgery was abandoned. It has been fifteen years since the onset of the disease, and now her abdomen is even larger, making daily life difficult. On the 14th of this month, she returned to Qu Zhibu Hospital for treatment. Hospital Director Qu Zhibu personally performed the laparotomy and completely removed the growth from the woman's abdomen. She is expected to be discharged from the hospital in about ten days. According to what the hospital director told the National News Agency reporter yesterday, the condition is called an ovarian cyst. The yellow-red greasy liquid weighed 87 pounds and was placed in a medicine tank for display and reference. Qu also said that although this condition has been found at the Hong Kong Road Red Cross Hospital and the Baker Road Chiang Hospital, the growths were only about 30 pounds. He has never seen one this large, which is truly rare.

Rural Woman Abducted to Shanghai, Saved, Then Commits Suicide 143

Water Disaster Relief Association Telegrams Her Husband to Shanghai to Take Her Back; The Husband Arrives and She Commits Suicide in the Hospital

Yu Songshi, the 28-year-old wife of Yu Dingyuan from Wangdian, Jiaxing, Zhejiang, was suddenly abducted to Shanghai by a man named Zhang Mingshan (according to the woman) while visiting her mother's home. She was lodged in a local inn. Fearing that Zhang intended to sell her, she escaped a few days ago and sought help from the Yunann Road Renji Tang Water Disaster Relief Association. The association, after learning the facts, sent a telegram to her husband, Yu Dingyuan, to come to Shanghai to reunite with her, and sent the woman to the Haidongchun Hotel on Baixianqiao Road for temporary accommodation. However, the woman was so traumatized by the abduction that she committed suicide by hanging herself with a belt in the hotel that night. Fortunately, she was discovered and rescued by the tea attendant, and her life was saved. The hotel then reported the incident to the association by telephone. The association, upon receiving the report, took the woman back and sent her to the Aiwenniyi Road Mental Hospital with a letter and staff. Since the woman had attempted suicide, the hospital was instructed to pay special attention to her. Her husband, after receiving the telegram from the Water Disaster Relief Association, learned of his wife's whereabouts and came to Shanghai yesterday afternoon. He went to the association to take his wife back for a reunion. However, when her husband arrived at the association, the hospital suddenly telephoned, saying that the woman had committed suicide in the hospital. After receiving the call, the association instructed her husband to go to the hospital to arrange for the retrieval and burial.

Lawsuit over Wet Nurse's Lack of Milk 144

Failure to Return Wages After Leaving Without Permission; Employer Sues for Fraud and Breach of Trust

Zhu Jianren, a 34-year-old Cantonese woman residing at No. 517 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, is currently full-term pregnant. She was admitted to the Renhe Hospital at No. 36 Rue Moliere for delivery. On the 22nd of last month, she gave birth to a healthy baby girl, much to the family's delight. She entrusted Guo Tiaomei, a relative who is a lawyer, to hire a wet nurse from various matchmaking agencies to feed the baby. Guo Tiaomei first gathered more than ten wet nurses and had their milk, blood, and physique tested at the Renhe Hospital. The test results showed that only the young woman from Yangzhou, Wu, brought by the Jin matchmaking agency at No. 202 Avenue Joffre, was qualified in terms of milk, blood, and body. The rest were dismissed, and Wu was hired. After a three-day trial, the three parties, the employer, the wet nurse, and the matchmaking agency, agreed on a monthly salary of 7 yuan. The matchmaking agency issued a guarantee, and Wu was formally hired. However, Wu's milk suddenly stopped after feeding the baby for a week, and a dispute arose. Wu then left. Zhu Jianren, whose baby is not yet a month old, expressed dissatisfaction with the wet nurse Wu and the Jin matchmaking agency and entrusted lawyer Guo Tiaomei to file a lawsuit with the Criminal Court of the Special Court, accusing the Jin matchmaking agency and Wu of fraud and breach of trust, requesting an investigation and, as an ancillary civil lawsuit, seeking compensation for the paid wages, matchmaking fee, and hospital examination fee. Upon receiving the complaint, Judge Wang Wangxu of the Criminal Court summoned Zhou Nanshan (30 years old, from Suzhou), the owner of the Jin matchmaking agency, and Wu to the court yesterday. The plaintiff's lawyer stated the intent of the prosecution, saying that after the plaintiff gave birth, she hired a wet nurse from more than ten candidates. She heard that Wu's milk was thick and qualified, and the matchmaking agency identified her on the spot and hired her at a monthly salary of 7 yuan. At that time, Wu claimed that her family was poor and requested to be paid several months' wages in advance to settle her family so that she could feed the baby with peace of mind. She asked to be paid five months' wages, and the plaintiff agreed to pay 35 yuan. However, after being hired for three or four days, Wu's milk suddenly stopped. When asked, Wu also requested to have eel, meat, dishes, and tonics to stimulate milk production. The employer agreed to provide them. However, the milk still did not increase much. The hospital's head nurse, Miss Liu, and others discovered that Wu was secretly throwing away the milk in the middle of the night. They negotiated with the matchmaking agency, but they shirked responsibility. They demanded that Wu return the wages and hire another wet nurse, but Wu refused to return the wages. They asked her to work as a nanny to offset the wages paid, but Wu also refused. Later, the matchmaking agency took Wu away. This shows that the defendants intended to commit fraud and breach of trust and should be punished according to the law. They requested that the ancillary civil lawsuit be approved and that the paid wages of five months, totaling 35 yuan, the doctor's examination fee of 6 yuan and 2 jiao, and the matchmaking fee of 5 yuan and 6 jiao, totaling 46 yuan and 8 jiao, be borne by the two defendants. They also presented the guarantee issued by the matchmaking agency as evidence. Zhou Nanshan, the owner of the Jin matchmaking agency, confessed that he had guaranteed the wet nurse. He only collected two months' wages at the time, which is the regulation set by various matchmaking agencies in Shanghai. He did not collect five months' wages. He said that Guo, the lawyer, came to hire the wet nurse, and his employee, surnamed Ge, sent Wu there. Later, due to the lack of milk, lawyer Guo came to negotiate with him. He replied that the matchmaking agency only guarantees against the wet nurse's escape or unexpected events. Lack of milk is not something he could say. He also told the employer that they wanted Wu to return the money, but Wu could not afford to return it. Lawyer Guo insisted on returning the money and pushed him and Wu out the door and closed the door. At that time, he thought the matter was over and Wu had returned to Yangzhou. Later, he received a summons and called Wu to Shanghai. Wu confessed that she only received one month's wages, which she used to pay the matchmaking fee and send her child home. The reason for the lack of milk was that it was not enough for the child to eat. She did not throw away the milk. The official showed Wu's guarantee, which stated that she had received five months' wages, 35 yuan, to Zhou Nanshan. After reading it, Zhou said that the numbers "five months, 35 yuan" were not written by his employee, surnamed Ge. He called his employee Ge Acheng, who was in the audience, to look at it. Ge also said that these numbers were not written by him, but the rest was written by him, and that the handwriting could be compared. The plaintiff's lawyer said that the guarantee was written by the defendant himself. The court then ordered the debate to begin and announced that the sentence would be pronounced at 2:00 PM on the 22nd.

Incoming Correspondence

The Path to Political Reform (Continued) 147

— Pan Gongzhan

(November 1935, Shanghai)

—Respectfully dedicated to the comrades of the Fifth National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang and gentlemen who are interested in discussing political reform—

(3) Given the vast territory and large population of the country, it is impossible for all members of the Kuomintang to directly exercise "political power." The National Assembly as stipulated in the Constitution remains a representative and deliberative body for exercising "political power." To enable the Kuomintang to lead the people in exercising "political power" during the transitional period, the election of National Assembly representatives can draw on the established practices of Russia, Italy, and Germany. Referring also to the election methods of previous Kuomintang National Congresses, the following two methods should be adopted in the representative election law after determining the number of representatives based on the population proportion of each county, city, and district: (a) The Kuomintang nominates twice the number of candidates in each city, county, and district, not limited to party members, and allows voters to elect them; (b) Voters in each city, county, and district elect twice the number of candidates, naturally also not limited to party members, and submits them to the Kuomintang for decision.

(4) Since the National Assembly is still a deliberative body, the Constitution should stipulate a clause stating, "The National Assembly represents all the people in collectively managing political power, organized by the following National Representatives." The powers of election, recall, initiative, and referendum it holds should also be appropriately defined. I believe that to clearly delineate "political power" and "governing power" and to centralize the responsibility for exercising governing power, the National Assembly's electoral and recall powers should only apply to the President and Vice President. As for the heads of the five Yuan (branches of government), the President can nominate candidates and appoint them after obtaining the consent of the National Assembly, holding them responsible to the National Assembly. Furthermore, the National Assembly's power to impeach the President should be limited to cases of illegal conduct. Regarding policy issues, the National Assembly can only pass resolutions requesting the President to dismiss the Premier of the Executive Yuan to express its disapproval. Of course, the President also has the power to dismiss the heads of the five Yuan. Speaking of the power of initiative, the National Assembly should have the power to directly enact complete legislation, but the President should also have the power to return it for reconsideration. As for the power of referendum, in addition to the National Assembly itself having the power to hold a referendum on legislation passed by the Legislative Yuan, the President or the Legislative Yuan should also be able to submit legislation passed, rejected, or unable to be established by the Legislative Yuan to the National Assembly for a referendum.

(5) The term of office for National Representatives should be four years. The National Assembly should convene once a year, with a session limited to one month, which may be extended by one month if necessary. If the President deems it necessary, or if one-third or more of the National Representatives deem it necessary, a special session of the National Assembly may be convened. In this way, during the recess of the National Assembly, it is not necessary to establish a "standing committee" to act as its representative. (To be continued)

An Overview of the Wool and Yarn Industry in Shanghai 148

— Edited by the China Credit Information Service

(Shanghai Industry and Commerce Overview, Part 2)

I. The Two Major Stages of the Wool and Yarn Industry in Shanghai

The raw materials for clothing in China have traditionally been limited to three types of textiles: cotton, silk, and hemp. However, since the late Qing Dynasty, urban and rural residents have not only utilized newly imported wool and woolen fabrics but have also learned to enjoy using wool yarn to knit clothing, socks, gloves, and the like. The content of people's lives has certainly become richer, but the power of foreign merchants has also grown as a result.

Wool yarn is commonly referred to as "mao leng" (毛冷). It is primarily made from spun wool and is a good raw material for winter clothing. Initially, the Chinese did not know how to imitate it, and it was entirely imported from overseas. During the late Qing Dynasty and the early Republic of China, those in Shanghai who sold these imported goods were mostly general stores that also sold cotton or hemp ropes. Their scale was small and they could not form an industry. Later, woolen knitwear gradually became popular inland, and sales grew daily, yielding substantial profits. Specialized wool yarn shops in Shanghai flourished, and today, Xingsheng Street in the French Concession has long become "Wool Yarn Street," the main base for the industry. There are nearly ten businesses of the same type there, and twenty businesses have joined the trade association, most of which combine retail and wholesale. Among them, Jin Yuanmao and Longxingchang have a longer history and more developed businesses. Although department stores also sell wool yarn, they are not as concentrated and extensive as the shops on Xingsheng Street.

As mentioned earlier, wool yarn is an imported product. The largest importer is the United Kingdom. The Bee brand wool yarn produced by Patons & Baldwins in the UK is particularly well-known and widely used by the Chinese. Here is a table listing the import amounts for the most recent three years and the first three quarters of this year for reference:

| | 1932 | 1933 | 1934 | First Three Quarters of 1935 |

| -------------------- | ------------ | ------------ | ------------ | ----------------------------- |

| United Kingdom | 5,165,773 | 4,42,497 | 4,4180,421 | Not Available |

| Other Countries | 2,435,53 | 21,206,853 | 2,302,602 | Not Available |

| Total | 7,601,295 | 6,618,350 | 6,483,023 | 1,105,985 |

Note: Figures are based on customs trade reports, in customs gold units.

The import of wool yarn in the first three quarters of 1935 is significantly lower than in the same period last year, likely because Patons & Baldwins has established a branch factory in Shanghai. Therefore, in essence, the UK remains the leading importer of wool yarn.

Shanghai is an important hub for industry and commerce nationwide, and the wool yarn trade is no exception. Therefore, in terms of customs districts, Shanghai accounts for a large proportion of wool yarn imports. See the table below:

Comparison Table of Wool Yarn Imports by Customs District for the Last Three Years

| | 1932 | 1933 | 1934 |

| ---------------- | ----------- | ----------- | ----------- |

| Shanghai | 5,256,367 | 5,169,556 | 5,341,599 |

| Other Customs Districts | 2,344,928 | 1,448,794 | 1,096,424 |

| Total | 7,601,295 | 6,618,350 | 6,438,023 |

Note: Same as above.

The period for ordering wool yarn in Shanghai is generally around the Lunar New Year. At that time, the sales for the year are completely determined, and businesses can use this information to gauge sales for the coming year and set their order targets. Most businesses entrust their orders to foreign firms, such as Dete, Baohua, Xiangchen, and Lihe, all of which engage in the trade. In the past, most of the Bee brand wool yarn was ordered through the EWO, Jardine, and Zhonghe firms before manufacturing. The goods generally arrive in May or June of the following year. Sales to other regions end after September. Wool yarn sales from Shanghai can be divided into three regions: the Pearl River, the Yangtze River, and North China. Before the September 18th Incident, Northeast China was also a large market. This is a general overview of the wool yarn trade in Shanghai.

The wool yarn industry in Shanghai can be divided into two major stages: purely trading and manufacturing combined with trading. The former has already been described, and we will now proceed to discuss how it entered the manufacturing stage.

Wool yarn is essentially a light industrial product, and imitation is not difficult. The only real obstacle is the raw material. In recent years, Chinese people have recognized the substantial achievements in the development of wool in the Northwest region. Furthermore, because wool yarn has long been imported from overseas, resulting in significant losses, they have started setting up factories to manufacture it themselves in an attempt to recover the lost profits. There are two companies in Tianjin, Dongya and Xianghe, and five in Shanghai, including Zhenxing Zhanghua (which has now stopped spinning wool yarn) and Shanghai Yumin China. They show promising signs of continued growth. The concern is that Patons & Baldwins of the UK, due to increased tariffs on wool yarn in China, established a factory in Shanghai last year to avoid customs barriers. With its strong capital and advanced technology, it poses a significant threat to the nascent wool yarn industry in China. (To be continued)

Financial Committee of the China Education Foundation Decides to Allocate Funds for Compulsory Education in Detail 151

An amount of 37,500 yuan will be allocated every two months.

Sun Hongfen said that paying in installments would not be a major difficulty.

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) The Board of Directors of the China Education and Culture Foundation, funded by the American Boxer Indemnity, previously resolved to subsidize compulsory education expenses nationwide with 300,000 yuan, to be allocated over two years at 150,000 yuan per year, in response to a request from the Ministry of Education regarding funding for compulsory education nationwide. However, the Foundation is experiencing financial difficulties and can only raise 70,000 yuan at present. The remaining amount will be discussed by the Finance Committee to determine fundraising methods. Xu Xinliu, Baker, and Hu Shi, members of the Finance Committee and Executive Committee stationed in Beijing and Shanghai, returned to Beijing immediately to convene a meeting. Due to business commitments, committee members Xu Xinliu and Baker were unable to come to Beijing. Executive Committee member Hu Shi arrived in Beiping this morning. The China Education Foundation convened a meeting of the Finance Committee at its meeting hall at 4:00 PM this afternoon.

Meeting Details

At the time, Director-General Sun Hongfen, former Director-General Ren Hongjun, accountants Zhou Yichun and Jin Shuchu, and Executive Committee representative Hu Shi, totaling five people, were present. Director-General Sun Hongfen chaired the meeting. The chairman first reported on the purpose of convening the meeting, stating that the Foundation's previous general meeting resolved to subsidize compulsory education expenses nationwide with 300,000 yuan. However, the Foundation is facing economic difficulties, and the issue of how to allocate these funds and how to raise the shortfall urgently needs to be resolved. Therefore, the Finance Committee was convened today to ask everyone to express their opinions. The discussion then began.

Funding Allocation Method

Regarding the method of allocating the 300,000 yuan subsidy for compulsory education expenses nationwide, after an exchange of opinions among the committee members, the following was decided: The subsidy of 300,000 yuan, as resolved by the previous general meeting, was to be allocated over two years. Now, due to economic difficulties, it was decided to adopt a method of allocating funds in installments, allocating the 300,000 yuan subsidy in eight installments, allocating 37,500 yuan every two months. A detailed consultation was also held on the Foundation's routine financial issues. The meeting adjourned at around 6:00 PM.

Sun Hongfen's Remarks

According to an interview with Director-General Sun Hongfen by a reporter: (1) The Foundation has decided to allocate the 300,000 yuan subsidy for compulsory education expenses nationwide in eight installments, allocating four times per year. This is a method devised to address the Foundation's financial difficulties. I anticipate that allocating the funds in this way, due to the small amount, may not cause major difficulties. The first batch of funds to be allocated may be disbursed by the end of this month or early next month. In short, since the Foundation has agreed to the Ministry of Education's subsidy for compulsory education expenses with 300,000 yuan, the Foundation will find a way to disburse the funds on schedule, no matter how difficult the finances are. (2) The Foundation advocates for specialized academic research and has established a "Cooperative Research Special Fund Committee" with Peking University. The Foundation and Peking University each contribute a portion of the funds annually, deposited in a bank. When either party needs funds, they can overdraw from this deposit. President Jiang (Menglin) serves as the chairman of the Cooperative Research Committee. This is the fifth year of the fund. This year, the China Education Foundation deposited 200,000 yuan and Peking University deposited 100,000 yuan. It is said that Peking University is currently distributing 7,500 yuan in student aid from the previous year to the various colleges, which will be overdrawn from this deposit, and the Foundation has been notified.

Marine Animal Collection Group of the Peiping Research Institute Discovers Cephalodiscus in Qingdao 152

This worm is intermediate between higher and lower animals.

Over 1,000 jars of marine animals were collected this time.

(Special Dispatch from Peiping) The Zoology Institute of the National Peiping Research Institute, in cooperation with the Qingdao Municipal Government, formed the "Jiaozhou Bay Marine Animal Collection Group" this spring. They went to Qingdao on May 1 for the first collection and again on September 27 for the second collection. The work has been completed, and the collected items have been transported to Beiping. The staff has also returned to Beiping. According to an interview with Zhang Xi, the head of the group, as follows:

Collection Scope

This trip to Jiaozhou Bay for collection was the second phase of work since the establishment of our group. The participants included Gu Guangzhong, Xiang Juli, Liu Yongbin, Kang Letian, and myself, all from the Zoology Institute of the Peiping Research Institute. We went to Qingdao on September 27 and completed the work on November 2, totaling 37 days. Excluding travel time, the actual work was only one month. The collection area was still within Jiaozhou Bay and the nearby coast. Because the Shandong Peninsula is quite important for Chinese marine animals, we used Qingdao as a research center for work convenience.

New Discoveries

We collected approximately 1,000 jars of marine animals this time. The harvest was different from the first collection because the last time was in spring and this time was in autumn. Marine animals often vary due to different seasons, so what we obtained in spring and autumn cannot be completely the same. The biggest gain this time was finding three species of Cephalodiscus and different species of Cephalodiscus. This Cephalodiscus occupies an important position in the biological world because it is intermediate between higher and lower animals. However, because this type of animal is mostly hidden in the seabed sand and rocks, it is very difficult to collect. We were very pleased to have obtained so many as three species this time. As for other new discoveries, they will have to wait until we open the boxes and study them one by one before we can determine them.

Collection Next Year

Because our group has a cooperative relationship with the Qingdao Municipal Government, we will still go to collect next year. This year's work will end here. Next year, we will collect at most three times, and at least two times. Whether we will extend the work after collecting next year is difficult to predict at this moment because the Qingdao Municipal Government stipulates that the collection work be completed within two years. (Jin)

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Orders County Education Bureaus to Seriously Implement Health Education 154

All Should Organize Health Education Committees

Issuing a First-Step Work Schedule for Compliance

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education yesterday issued instructions to the education bureaus of 60 counties, including Zhenjiang, Shanghai, Songjiang, and Baoshan, stating: "In order to promote health education, the Provincial Health Education Committee was specifically organized, and a work outline was formulated. The second meeting decided that the bureaus should be notified to handle the matter. Currently, it has been found that some counties have organized committees to handle health education matters, while others are directly handled by the bureaus. Some have organized health education committees or health education guidance committees. The responsibilities are not defined, and the names are also very diverse, which is an obstacle to the future of promotion. Based on the recommendation of the Jiangsu Provincial Health Education Committee, please order all counties to organize county health education committees immediately, with the health education instructors of each bureau as the center, and under the leadership of the educational authorities, to be responsible for handling all county health education promotion matters. All health education committees or health education guidance committees that have been organized but have different names should be uniformly corrected to be consistent. In addition, a seven-item table of first-step work has been drafted, and the recommendation of each council has been reviewed, all of which are essential and feasible. Compliance should be ordered. In addition to separate orders, urgently issue a seven-item table of first-step work, ordering the bureau chiefs to supervise the health education instructors and seriously handle the matter. The organization of the health education committees in each county should refer to the organization of the Provincial Health Education Committee, and the compliance should be reported at any time for inspection and review. The attached list of first-step work items for health education in each county is as follows: (1) Hold health lectures, (2) Show health education films, (3) Guide children's hygiene habits, (4) Examine children's physical condition, (5) Vaccinations, (6) First aid knowledge drills, (7) Hold health education talks for parents."

Educational Institutions in Various Provinces and Cities Promote the Ministry's Simplified Character Implementation Measures 155

New Elementary School Textbooks from July Next Year

Those Not Using the Ministry's Simplified Characters Will Not be Approved

The first batch of simplified characters, totaling 324, has already been announced by the Ministry of Education. The implementation measures for educational administrative organs in various provinces and cities have also been stipulated as follows: (1) All elementary school, short-term elementary school, and mass school textbooks, children's and mass reading materials should use the Ministry's simplified characters. (2) Textbooks using the Ministry's simplified characters should include a vocabulary list at the back of each volume, incorporating the simplified characters, and a comparison table should be set up in the textbook where the character is first used or below or in other appropriate places for comparison. The table format is attached below. (3) From July 1936, newly compiled elementary school textbooks, short-term elementary school textbooks, or mass school textbooks that do not use the Ministry's simplified characters will not be approved. (4) From July 1936, all textbooks opened in the previous article should use the Ministry's simplified characters. (5) From July 1936, newly compiled or reprinted children's or mass reading materials that do not use the Ministry's simplified characters may not be used by schools. (6) From July 1936, all levels of normal schools should focus on teaching the Ministry's simplified characters. (7) From July 1936, in school exam answers, the Ministry's simplified characters may be used uniformly. (8) Newspapers in each province, city, and county should be persuaded by the local educational administrative organ to adopt the Ministry's simplified characters for printing within a possible range. (9) These measures will be implemented from the date of promulgation.

The Second List of Teachers Approved to Take the Compulsory Education Class Examination: Wang Dexiang, Chen Zongyu, Yang Hanchu, Huang Yuanding, Xu Gang, Yin Ruihe, Huang Bugao, Wang Qiliang, Lu Jinfan, Wan Chengyu, Zhang Junde, Zhao Yuping, Hu Baoren, Chen Zongtang, Zou Huilin, Chu Zhuo, Liu Ruojin, Huang Kezhang, Zhang Xiaomin, Ju Sihe, Ji Xianzhi, Liu Zan, Ji Xian, Wang Erxian, Shi Mengqing, Wei Shugao, Ding Pei, Li Renji, Mei Binghuan, Feng Bira, Chen Kaike.

Private Schools Transformed into Schools in Henan Province 157

Before the popularization of compulsory education, the Henan Provincial Education Administration temporarily allowed the establishment of private schools but urged them to improve and transform private schools into universal schools. The main points of the province's private school management measures are listed below: (1) All private schools established by private individuals or private associations, and private elementary schools that have not been approved for establishment, which aim to teach, are regarded as private schools. (2) Private schools should be named after the smallest local name in the area where they are located. At the beginning of each school year, a registration form must be filled out and submitted for record. (3) Private schools may not be established within three weeks of an elementary school, but if each class in the elementary school has more than 50 children, it may be allowed depending on the circumstances. (4) Private school teachers must be over 20 years old, of good character, support the Three Principles of the People, and have one of the following qualifications to be qualified: (a) Passed the elementary school teacher certification or private school teacher qualification examination, (b) Received normal education, (c) Graduated from a junior high school or above, (d) Served as an elementary school teacher for more than one year and has excellent performance as judged by inspectors. (5) Private schools should establish the following subjects: (a) Required subjects: Civics, Chinese, General Knowledge (including social studies, natural science, and hygiene), Arithmetic (abacus or written calculation), Work, (Physical education included), (b) Elective subjects: Needlework, Music. (6) The textbooks used in private schools should be those edited or approved by the Ministry of Education. Books that violate modern trends of thought and hinder the development of children's personality are not allowed to be taught. If there are students over the age of 20 with higher levels who are interested in classics and history, they are allowed to study automatically and submit the names of the books and people they are studying to the Education Bureau for record. (7) Private school teaching should adopt a group system. (8) Private schools must have at least the following facilities: (a) Sun Yat-sen's portrait, the national flag, (b) Blackboard, clock, bell or whistle, chalk, suitable desks and chairs, (c) Timetable, student register, grade book, abacus, (d) Appropriate sports equipment and drawing books such as textbooks, teaching books, dictionaries, reference books, etc. (e) A daily newspaper. (9) Private schools should hold ceremonies on the prescribed commemorative days, and may take holidays as appropriate during busy farming seasons, but the total number of holidays throughout the year may not exceed three months. (10) Private school teachers should treat children with sincerity and guidance and should not abuse corporal punishment. (11) Private schools may not accept students from nearby elementary schools. (12) The Education Bureau should refer to each private school at any time. If the management is not up to standard and does not improve after guidance, a warning will be given. If there is still no progress after two warnings, the school will be ordered to disband. (13) The Education Bureau should use the holidays to hold training courses for private school teachers and implement training.

Time: 6:30 PM to 7:00 PM

Frequency: 660 (Central Broadcasting Station)

Municipal Bureau of Education - Continued Review of Serial Comic Books 159

After consultation with the Bureau of Social Affairs and the Bureau of Public Safety

And ordering all bookstores in the city to comply

The serial comic books published by various bookstores in this city are mostly works of gods, monsters, obscenity, etc. Since the Bureau of Education began rectification the year before last, various new pictures have been improved day by day, and gradual results have been achieved. However, since the Book and Magazine Review Committee of the Central Propaganda Committee stopped working, no one has been responsible for reviewing the drafts, causing the attitude of the bookstores to revive, competing to print pictures of gods, monsters and obscenities, almost abandoning all previous efforts, which is a pity. Therefore, after consultation between the Bureau of Education and the Bureau of Social Affairs and the Bureau of Public Safety, it was decided that before the central review agency is reorganized and established, the Bureau of Education will still be responsible for presiding over the review work, and the Bureau of Social Affairs and the Bureau of Public Safety will assist in handling it. This method has been reported to the municipal government and has been ordered to all bookstores to comply, it is said.

Famous Speakers in the Department of Social Education, Great China University 162

Since the establishment of the Department of Social Education of Great China University in 1920, the content of the curriculum has been enriched and systematized through the planning of the former director, Ma Zongrong. This year, a course on film education has been added. Recently, because the central government has paid great attention to broadcast education, in order to increase students' knowledge of mechanical aspects, Hu Ruding, director of the Electrical Machinery Manufacturing Plant of the Construction Committee and director of the Department of Electrical Engineering of Zhejiang University, was specially invited to give a lecture on the mechanical installation of broadcast education at 5 pm this Monday. Two or three hundred students from the College of Education and the College of Science attended the lecture. Mr. Hu first described the 40-year brief history of radio development and its trend in our country, and pointed out its proper use. At present, there are more than 100 radio stations of all sizes in the country, with the Central Broadcasting Station being the largest with 75 kilowatts, ranking second in the world. Next, he described the structure and functions of the large-scale domestic radio receiver he brought from the factory. The evaluation of the radio receiver is based on the two most important conditions of selectivity and publicity or credibility. The trend of its structure does not necessarily determine the quality by the number of vacuum tubes and bulbs, but rather the improvement of other parts. He also distributed the instruction manual for the Jiandian No. 58 radio, which is specially designed for use in empty and remote places without power supply, and has the four major characteristics of long reception distance, power saving, accurate sound, and easy repair. Finally, the students asked questions and Mr. Hu answered them one by one, and everyone dispersed happily at 6 o'clock.

On the same day, at 8 o'clock in the morning, the study class of the department also invited Huang Jingwan, director of the Automobile Department and Doctor of Diplomacy of the Commercial Press, to lecture on the structure and usage of the automobile library. Mr. Huang prepared sufficient supporting evidence and cited in an orderly and logical manner. He first described the development of mobile maps in China, and then described the history of automobile invention and its cooperation with books and the various benefits. The listeners were all very interested, it is said.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (100) 164

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"I don't mind; but if I feel a little inconvenient, I would like to give you those drawers, because I value the treasures of children, and I think they should be respected and cherished. Don, I am now willing to make a deal with you. I hope you can keep your credit. Here are twelve drawers, one for each month, just enough for a year. If you can fulfill some of your little responsibilities, then you can earn a few, and those few will be yours. I believe that certain types of rewards are especially for young people; they can help us move forward. We initially try to be good for the sake of rewards, but if used properly, we will soon be happy to be good regardless of other things."

"Do you also have rewards?" Don asked, looking as if he had never heard the above words.

"Of course, I can't do without them. But my rewards are not drawers, or gifts, or more days off, but also what I love very much, just as you love those things. The good character and success of my students are one of my beloved rewards. I try to get it, just as I want you to work hard to get that cabinet. Forcing yourself to do what you don't like to do, and doing it well, then you can get two rewards—first, the prize that you can see and touch; the other is the joy of fulfilling a responsibility happily. Do you understand this?"

"Yes, ma'am."

The Money Shops' Allocation of Head Quotas is Ineffective 183

Recently, since the implementation of the legal tender policy, the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and Central Bank have issued head quotas in legal tender daily. Previously, these quotas were allocated to the money shops by these three banks. However, since legal tender issued downward can be used for payment without needing to be allocated from the money shops, the market has ample quotas, and there is no need to add water. The money shops, on the other hand, are suffering from the inability to allocate quotas. Even intra-industry allocations are proving difficult. The interbank call loan rate remains at one cent and three mils, unchanged from morning to afternoon. In the morning, over 3.2 million was transacted for account transfers, with over 400,000 in new transactions. In the afternoon, transactions amounted to 300,000. Transactions at the Smaller Banks Association totaled 600,000. Over 500,000 was used for the redemption of foreign pledges, with over 700,000 in new issuances. Spring and Autumn

Snippets 197

Some lonely people, living in desolate circumstances with no relatives or friends, often raise a cat or a dog in order to find some emotional support. Their love for the cat or dog is much deeper than that of ordinary people; it's almost like treating them as their own lover or children, showing that humans all possess great love, and this love is humanity's only beauty.

Young people certainly cannot lack love, because love is the fertilizer of youth. Therefore, when they have not found an ideal lover, they often feel disoriented and desolate, as if traveling in a desert, even to the point of suffering illness. When they finally find an ideal lover, it's naturally like receiving sweet dew in extreme hunger and thirst. But in this beautiful realm of love, you must not think that it is your final destination. That is to say, you must not forget your own and society's future. You must know that a person who truly understands love and uses it well must expand love from the narrow confines to all of humanity.

In the hearts of Chinese people, the hardest kind of love to find is love for the country. This is one of the greatest shortcomings of the Chinese people, and it is the reason why they suffer. The crux of the matter is that Chinese people only know the benevolence of their parents and do not know that the country is even more benevolent; they only know the beauty of their lover and do not know that the country is even more beautiful.

Memorial Arch 198

— Qiao Yunsi

The iron statue of Song Qin Hui by West Lake is a representation of punishing evil, rooting out treachery, and leaving behind a lasting infamy. Conversely, building a memorial archway to leave a fragrance for eternity is a symbol of honoring virtue and rewarding merit. Our Chinese nation is inherently a land of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame. How did we used to honor loyal officials, filial sons, chaste widows, and virtuous women? We often erected stone memorial archways as models for later generations. The essence of this lies in the loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, righteousness, harmony, and peace that the current leaders emphasize. In the imperial examination era, fame, position, and wealth were often also displayed on a memorial archway, revealing the social status of the person being honored. For example, even if someone was a successful candidate in the imperial exam, the palace examination and selection would result in those in first place receiving the distinction of "Presented Scholar, Grade A" - this memorial archway would be erected on your behalf by the state. The second and third places, with the distinctions of "Presented Scholar" and "Of Presented Scholar Origin," would not have the same prominence as the first place. In general, these memorial archways were similar to today's bronze statues and memorial halls in that they had longevity. Since the founding of the Republic of China, for every grand celebration, memorial archways have been replaced with painted arches. Most of these are made of pine and cypress branches, adorned with gilded and resplendent large characters on decorative panels. This kind of embellishment for a time of peace and prosperity is treated like worn-out shoes after a short period in office, which is very much in line with the saying "building a house costs three stones of rice, demolishing a house costs one meal." However, because "the boundless scenery is all new at once," this is viewed as commonplace; it only allows bamboo craftsmen and florists to earn some extra income. Now that the times have evolved, the arches erected along the way for this 6th National Games are completely different from the past. They have already shattered the bamboo craftsmen and florists' side income, becoming the design of engineering experts. Although the framework is made of wood, the audience's perspective from afar makes it look like a three-dimensional building made of reinforced concrete. It is said that the cost of each is estimated at 500 yuan. Its purpose is also different from the simple aspirations of the past. It is not just adding color to the games themselves, but another group singing the greatness of this feat. Its side effect is even more "advertisement" on "page two."

Clerk 199

— Shi Songshan

Just for the recruitment of a clerk who only needs to be able to write a few neat characters and have slightly fluent writing skills, there are so many applicants because of the monthly salary of twenty yuan.

Since I came out of my mother's womb, I have never held a job. Counting it, it's been almost thirty years, but I am increasingly unwilling to loaf around. I really don't have any opportunities. Fortunately, I still have some remaining assets, but eventually, sitting and eating empties the mountain, so I now have to seek a position by any means necessary because my life cannot allow me to continue drifting along.

I am very satisfied with a salary of twenty yuan a month, so I mustered my courage and decided to apply.

The unlucky star hadn't left yet, and it wasn't very auspicious. As soon as I ran out the door, rain suddenly poured down from the sky, and I didn't have any rain gear. I was afraid that I would be late and miss the application time, so I decided to brave the rain. When I arrived, I was soaking wet, as if I had taken a bath. My originally faded blue cloth gown would surely have many more stains this time.

An old gentleman, about fifty years old, with a shiny bald head, was probably the principal. He was very kind and spoke with a smile on the corner of his mouth, perhaps because he knew the distress of the unemployed, so he treated us so sincerely.

There were five test questions, and we were required to submit the papers by 11:40 AM. After many of us finished the exam, the old gentleman busily greeted us with a smile on his face and invited us to the dining hall to eat, saying, "Please have a meal of hardship." I thought, after all, the elders have experience and never act condescendingly. If it were a young man in Western clothes, he would probably have a different face.

All applicants will hear news within three days. If no news is received within the specified date, there is no need to have any illusions. I waited as if I were waiting for an official verdict, but with so many people, choosing one person, my hopes are not very optimistic, but I am still waiting for news.

Time slipped by quickly, and three days had already passed. I had already given up on this idea. Just for the recruitment of a clerk, there are so many applicants. Choosing one person from among so many, naturally the best will be chosen. There must be such talent, but it just wasn't my turn.
